Infallibility of All Angels and Refutation of Objections
Commentator affirms angelic infallibility and refutes two apparent objections.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the consensus on the infallibility of all angels and how to interpret the Quranic objection (Q2:30) and the story of Harut and Marut.

Core Idea
All angels are infallible; objections and questionable stories are baseless.

This lesson addresses the well-known position that all angels are preserved from sin. The commentator explains that the angels' question in the Quran is not a complaint but a request for wisdom, and the story of Harut and Marut is a fabrication.

Guided Path
1
Affirm angelic infallibility
The passage states that the well-known position (المشهور) is the infallibility of all angels. This is the established Sunni view.
2
Analyze the angels' question in Q2:30
The verse 'Will You place therein...' might be misunderstood as a criticism. The commentator clarifies it is merely an inquiry (استفهام), not backbiting or objection.
This respects the angels' perfect obedience.
3
Refute the Harut and Marut story
The commentator dismisses the story as inauthentic, saying it is a fabrication of the Jews. Some scholars say they were righteous men called angels metaphorically.
This preserves the doctrine of angelic sinlessness.

And al-Bari is the Creator, from al-bar' meaning creation. It may be said that the protection of the prophets was already mentioned in his statement: 'And obligatory upon them is trustworthiness,' since trustworthiness is protection. It may be answered that he mentioned it here in order to include the angels with the prophets in its ruling and being described by it. And 'isma linguistically is absolute preservation, and technically is God's preservation of the morally responsible person from sin such that its occurrence is impossible. It is not permissible for us to ask for 'isma in this technical sense, such as saying 'O God, we ask you for protection.' Commentary
This passage continues the discussion of 'isma. The commentator first explains the word 'al-Bari' (the Creator). He then addresses a potential redundancy: that the prophets' 'isma was already mentioned earlier in the poem under the attribute of trustworthiness (amana). The answer is that the poet re-mentions it here to explicitly include angels in the same ruling. Next, the commentator defines 'isma both linguistically (absolute preservation) and technically (God's preservation of the morally responsible person from sin such that it is impossible to commit). However, asking in the linguistic sense (general preservation) is permissible. Then, the commentator affirms the well-known position that all angels are infallible. He explains the verse 'Will You place therein...' (Q. 2:30) is not a reproach or objection but a simple inquiry. He also refutes the story of Harut and Marut as fabricated by Jews and unreliable. Some say they were two righteous men called angels metaphorically. A footnote adds that al-Zamakhshari affirmed the 'isma of Maryam.

The Qualified Superiority of the Four Caliphs and Ten over Angels
Clarifies the scope of human superiority over angels.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the four caliphs and the ten companions are superior only to common angels, not to angelic leaders like Jibril.

Core Idea
The caliphs and ten companions outrank common angels, but not the angelic leaders.

The poet's statement about the superiority of the four caliphs and the ten promised paradise over the angels of Badr might seem absolute, but a careful reading reveals an important qualification. This lesson unpacks that qualification, showing how it aligns with the broader principle that angelic leaders are superior to ordinary humans.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the key phrase 'on other than their leaders'.
The passage is a clarification, not a new ruling.
2
Identify the qualification
The poet's claim applies only to angels who are not leaders. Understand the reason: because angelic leaders are superior to common humans.
3
Understand the analogy
The same logic applies to the angels who witnessed Badr (they are better than other angels) and by analogy to believing jinn.
The analogy shows consistency in ranks.
4
Reflect on the principle
This passage teaches that ranks in creation are hierarchical and qualified; we must not oversimplify comparisons.
It guards against the misconception that all angels are inferior to these humans.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم إنَّ ما اقتضاه كلام الناظم من أن الأربعة الخلفاء والستة الذين هم تمام العشرة أفضلُ من الملائكة الذين هم حضروا بدراً .. محمول على غير رؤسائهم؛ لما تقدَّم من أن رؤساءهم أفضل من عوام البشر، وقد علمت أن المراد بهم أولياؤهم كأبي بكر وعمر ثم الملائكة الذين شهدوا بدراً أفضل ممن لم يشهدها منهم، وقياسه أن يقال: كذلك في مؤمني الجن.
Then indeed, what is necessitated by the words of the poet — that the four caliphs and the six who complete the ten are better than the angels who attended Badr — is carried upon other than their leaders; because it has preceded that their leaders are better than the common people of humanity, and you have known that what is intended by them is their close ones like Abu Bakr and 'Umar. Then the angels who witnessed Badr are better than those who did not witness it from among them, and by analogy it is said: likewise among the believing jinn.
Source pages p. 302

Commentary
This passage is a clarification regarding the rank of the four caliphs and the ten companions (the ten who were promised Paradise). The poet's statement that they are better than the angels who attended the Battle of Badr is interpreted as referring only to angels who are not leaders (i.e., not the archangels or chief angels). The reasoning is based on the established principle that the leaders of the angels (e.g., Jibril, Mika'il, etc.) are superior to the common righteous humans. Therefore, the caliphs and the ten are better than the common angels, not the angelic leaders. The same analogy is applied to believing jinn who attended Badr—they are better than other jinn but not superior to angelic leaders.

Correction: The poet's statement applies only to angels who are not leaders; angelic leaders are superior.

Increase in Lifespan: Goodness or Relative to Angels' Scrolls?
Al-Ujhuri explains the concept of increase in lifespan and its interpretations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two explanations for increase in lifespan and how it relates to what is recorded in the angels' scrolls versus God's eternal knowledge.

Core Idea
Increase in lifespan is relative to the angels' scrolls, not to God's unchanging knowledge.

This lesson examines a key theological concept: how can we speak of an increase in lifespan if God's knowledge is immutable? The author presents two interpretations—one of increase in goodness and blessing, and another relative to the scrolls of the angels. The example of Zayd clarifies the distinction between absolute and conditional recordings.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its translation to get the gist.
Notice the reference to the hadith at the start.
2
Identify the two interpretations
Look for the words 'بحسب الخير والبركة' and 'بسبة لما ثبت في صحف الملائكة'. These are the two ways increase is understood.
3
Analyze the example of Zayd
The example illustrates how the same lifespan can be recorded differently in the angels' scrolls (absolutely) and in God's knowledge (conditionally). Understand the condition: if he obeys, he gets sixty; otherwise fifty.
This example resolves the apparent contradiction between the hadith and God's foreknowledge.
4
Connect to the hadith
The hadith about maintaining family ties is cited as evidence that actions can affect what is recorded in the angels' scrolls.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
خیر آحاد (۱) ، أو أن الزيادة فيه بحسب الخير والبركة، أو بالنسبة لما ثبت في صحف الملائكة، فقد يثبت الشيء فيها مطلقاً، وهو في علم الله تعالى مقيدٌ مقيد)، كأن يكون في صحف الملائكة : إن عمر زيد خمسون مثلاً مطلقاً، وهو في علم الله تعالى مُقيَّد بالا يفعل كذا من الطاعات، وإن فعلها فله ستون (۳) ، فإن سبق في علمه تعالى أنه يفعلها فلا يتخلَّف عن فعلها وكان عمره ستين فالزيادة بحسب الظاهر على ما في صحف الملائكة، وإلا فلا بد من تحقق ما في علمه تعالى كما يشير له قوله تعالى: ﴿يَمْحُوا الله مَا يَشَاءُ وَيُنْبِتُ وَعِندَهُ أُمُّ الْكِتِبِ﴾ [الرعد: ۳۹]؛ أي : أصل اللوح المحفوظ ؛ وهو علمه تعالى الذي لا محو فيه ولا إثبات، وأما اللوح المحفوظ فالحق قبول ما فيه للمحو والإثبات كصحف الملائكة، وبعضهم فسَّر أم الكتاب باللوح المحفوظ ؛ لأنه ما من كائن إلا وهو مكتوب فيه والراجح الأول
(1) أخرج البخاري (٣٠٦٧) ، ومسلم (٢٥٥٧) عن أنس بن مالك رضي الله عنه قال : سمعت رسول الله يقول: «من سره أن يبسط له في رزقه أو يُنسأ له في أثره، فليصل رحمه .
(۲) قوله (وهو في علم الله مقيد . إلى آخره) بيان ذلك أن الله يعلم أزلاً أن زيداً يطيع، وأن له ذلك من العمر ستين سنة، ويعلم أيضاً أنه لو لم يطع لكان عمره خمسين سنة، وهذا هو معنى كون ما في صحف الملائكة مُقيَّداً في علم الله بألا يفعل كذا من الطاعات، وليس المراد من التقييد التعليق، بل المراد منه ما تقدَّم من أنه لو لم يطلع لكان عمره خمسين سنة مثلاً، سنة مثلاً، ويحمل التقييد على هذا المعنى اندفع ما يتراءى من العبارة من أنَّ علم الله مشوب بالتردد. انتهى أجهوري.
(۳) قوله : ( وإن فعلها قله (ستون) أي: وفي علم الله أنه إن فعلها فله ستون سنة، ومعنى ذلك : أن الله تعالى يعلم أن جعل عمره ستين سنة مرتب على طاعته المقطوع بوقوعها في علم الله، وبهذا اندفع ما توهمه العبارة من كون علم الله مشوباً بالتردد. انتهى أجهوري.
The best of individuals (1), or that the increase in it is according to goodness and blessing, or relative to what is established in the scrolls of the angels. For a thing may be established in them absolutely, while it is in the knowledge of Allah Most High restricted (restricted), such that it is in the scrolls of the angels: 'Indeed the lifespan of Zayd is fifty years, for example, absolutely,' while it is in the knowledge of Allah Most High restricted to his not doing such-and-such acts of obedience, and if he does them, he has sixty (3). If it preceded in His knowledge that he would do them, then he will not fail to do them and his lifespan will be sixty, so the increase is apparent relative to what is in the scrolls of the angels. Otherwise, there must be realization of what is in His knowledge, as His statement indicates: 'Allah erases what He wills and confirms, and with Him is the Mother of the Book' [13:39]; that is, the origin of the Preserved Tablet; and it is His knowledge, which has no erasing nor confirming in it. As for the Preserved Tablet, it is subject to erasing and confirming in it, like the scrolls of the angels. And some interpreted the Mother of the Book as the Preserved Tablet, because nothing exists except it is written in it, and the preponderant view is the first.
(1) Al-Bukhari (3067) and Muslim (2557) narrated from Anas ibn Malik that he said: I heard the Messenger of Allah say: 'Whoever wishes that his provision be expanded and his lifespan be prolonged, let him maintain family ties.'
(2) His statement: 'while it is in the knowledge of Allah restricted... to the end' — the explanation of that is that Allah knows eternally that Zayd will obey, and that he has from that a lifespan of sixty years, and He also knows that if he had not obeyed, his lifespan would have been fifty years. This is the meaning of what is in the scrolls of the angels being restricted in Allah's knowledge to his not doing such-and-such acts of obedience. The intended meaning of restriction is not suspension, but rather what has preceded that if he did not do it, his lifespan would have been fifty years, for example, and by interpreting restriction in this sense, what appears from the expression that Allah's knowledge is mixed with hesitation is repelled. End of al-Ujhuri.
(3) His statement: 'and if he does them, he has sixty' — that is, in Allah's knowledge that if he does them, he has sixty years. The meaning of that is that Allah Most High knows that making his lifespan sixty years is contingent upon his obedience that is definitively occurring in Allah's knowledge, and by this, the suspicion that Allah's knowledge is mixed with hesitation is repelled. End of al-Ujhuri.
Source pages p. 328

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the concept of increase in lifespan. The author begins by explaining that the increase can be understood in multiple ways: either as an increase in goodness and blessing, or as an increase relative to what is written in the angels' scrolls. He provides an example: the scrolls may record Zayd's lifespan as fifty years absolutely, but in God's knowledge, it is restricted based on whether Zayd performs certain acts of obedience. If God knows that Zayd will perform them, his lifespan becomes sixty years. The author then discusses the verse from Surat al-Ra'd about erasing and confirming, distinguishing between the 'Mother of the Book' (Umm al-Kitab), which is God's eternal knowledge that never changes, and the Preserved Tablet (al-Lawh al-Mahfuz), which is subject to erasure and confirmation, similar to the angels' scrolls. Some scholars interpret Umm al-Kitab as the Preserved Tablet itself, but the author notes that the preponderant view is that it is God's knowledge. The footnotes elaborate on the restriction concept, emphasizing that God's knowledge is not subject to hesitation or change; the restriction is simply a recognition of what would happen under different conditions. The hadith about maintaining family ties is cited as evidence that actions can affect what is recorded in the angels' scrolls, but not God's eternal knowledge.

Key Terms
زيادة العمر
صحف الملائكة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That an increase in lifespan implies a change in God's knowledge.
Correction: The increase is relative to the angels' scrolls, not God's knowledge, which is immutable.

Checkpoint
What does the example of Zayd illustrate according to the passage?
A) That God's knowledge changes based on actions.
B) That the angels' scrolls record lifespans conditionally.
C) That actions can affect what is recorded in the angels' scrolls.
D) That all lifespans are fixed and unchangeable.

Key Takeaway
Increase in lifespan is understood as relative to the angels' scrolls, not to God's immutable knowledge, resolving an apparent contradiction with divine foreknowledge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Umm al-Kitab and the Preserved Tablet: Distinguishing Two Divine Records
Al-Ujhuri distinguishes Umm al-Kitab from the Preserved Tablet.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the difference between Umm al-Kitab (the Mother of the Book) and the Prescribed Tablet, and why the preponderant view is that Umm al-Kitab is God's eternal knowledge.

Core Idea
Umm al-Kitab is God's unchanging knowledge; the Preserved Tablet can be erased and confirmed, like the angels' scrolls.

This lesson unpacks the verse from Surah al-Ra'd that mentions erasing and confirming. The author explains two interpretations of 'Umm al-Kitab'—either it is the Preserved Tablet or it is God's eternal knowledge. The preponderant view, he states, is that it is God's knowledge, which undergoes no change.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation, focusing on the verse and its explanation.
2
Identify the key distinction
Notice the difference between 'Umm al-Kitab' (no erasure/confirmation) and the 'Preserved Tablet' (subject to erasure/confirmation).
The Preserved Tablet is like the angels' scrolls.
3
Understand the two interpretations
Some scholars interpret Umm al-Kitab as the Preserved Tablet. The author notes the preponderant view is that it is God's knowledge.
Think about why God's knowledge cannot be subject to change.
4
Connect to previous lesson
Relate this to the earlier discussion on lifespan increase: the angels' scrolls are mutable, while God's knowledge is immutable.

Source Text

خیر آحاد (۱) ، أو أن الزيادة فيه بحسب الخير والبركة، أو بالنسبة لما ثبت في صحف الملائكة، فقد يثبت الشيء فيها مطلقاً، وهو في علم الله تعالى مقيدٌ مقيد)، كأن يكون في صحف الملائكة : إن عمر زيد خمسون مثلاً مطلقاً، وهو في علم الله تعالى مُقيَّد بالا يفعل كذا من الطاعات، وإن فعلها فله ستون (۳) ، فإن سبق في علمه تعالى أنه يفعلها فلا يتخلَّف عن فعلها وكان عمره ستين فالزيادة بحسب الظاهر على ما في صحف الملائكة، وإلا فلا بد من تحقق ما في علمه تعالى كما يشير له قوله تعالى: ﴿يَمْحُوا الله مَا يَشَاءُ وَيُنْبِتُ وَعِندَهُ أُمُّ الْكِتِبِ﴾ [الرعد: ۳۹]؛ أي : أصل اللوح المحفوظ ؛ وهو علمه تعالى الذي لا محو فيه ولا إثبات، وأما اللوح المحفوظ فالحق قبول ما فيه للمحو والإثبات كصحف الملائكة، وبعضهم فسَّر أم الكتاب باللوح المحفوظ ؛ لأنه ما من كائن إلا وهو مكتوب فيه والراجح الأول
(1) أخرج البخاري (٣٠٦٧) ، ومسلم (٢٥٥٧) عن أنس بن مالك رضي الله عنه قال : سمعت رسول الله يقول: «من سره أن يبسط له في رزقه أو يُنسأ له في أثره، فليصل رحمه .
(۲) قوله (وهو في علم الله مقيد . إلى آخره) بيان ذلك أن الله يعلم أزلاً أن زيداً يطيع، وأن له ذلك من العمر ستين سنة، ويعلم أيضاً أنه لو لم يطع لكان عمره خمسين سنة، وهذا هو معنى كون ما في صحف الملائكة مُقيَّداً في علم الله بألا يفعل كذا من الطاعات، وليس المراد من التقييد التعليق، بل المراد منه ما تقدَّم من أنه لو لم يطلع لكان عمره خمسين سنة مثلاً، سنة مثلاً، ويحمل التقييد على هذا المعنى اندفع ما يتراءى من العبارة من أنَّ علم الله مشوب بالتردد. انتهى أجهوري.
(۳) قوله : ( وإن فعلها قله (ستون) أي: وفي علم الله أنه إن فعلها فله ستون سنة، ومعنى ذلك : أن الله تعالى يعلم أن جعل عمره ستين سنة مرتب على طاعته المقطوع بوقوعها في علم الله، وبهذا اندفع ما توهمه العبارة من كون علم الله مشوباً بالتردد. انتهى أجهوري.
The best of individuals (1), or that the increase in it is according to goodness and blessing, or relative to what is established in the scrolls of the angels. For a thing may be established in them absolutely, while it is in the knowledge of Allah Most High restricted (restricted), such that it is in the scrolls of the angels: 'Indeed the lifespan of Zayd is fifty years, for example, absolutely,' while it is in the knowledge of Allah Most High restricted to his not doing such-and-such acts of obedience, and if he does them, he has sixty (3). If it preceded in His knowledge that he would do them, then he will not fail to do them and his lifespan will be sixty, so the increase is apparent relative to what is in the scrolls of the angels. Otherwise, there must be realization of what is in His knowledge, as His statement indicates: 'Allah erases what He wills and confirms, and with Him is the Mother of the Book' [13:39]; that is, the origin of the Preserved Tablet; and it is His knowledge, which has no erasing nor confirming in it. As for the Preserved Tablet, it is subject to erasing and confirming in it, like the scrolls of the angels. And some interpreted the Mother of the Book as the Preserved Tablet, because nothing exists except it is written in it, and the preponderant view is the first.
(1) Al-Bukhari (3067) and Muslim (2557) narrated from Anas ibn Malik that he said: I heard the Messenger of Allah say: 'Whoever wishes that his provision be expanded and his lifespan be prolonged, let him maintain family ties.'
(2) His statement: 'while it is in the knowledge of Allah restricted... to the end' — the explanation of that is that Allah knows eternally that Zayd will obey, and that he has from that a lifespan of sixty years, and He also knows that if he had not obeyed, his lifespan would have been fifty years. This is the meaning of what is in the scrolls of the angels being restricted in Allah's knowledge to his not doing such-and-such acts of obedience. The intended meaning of restriction is not suspension, but rather what has preceded that if he did not do it, his lifespan would have been fifty years, for example, and by interpreting restriction in this sense, what appears from the expression that Allah's knowledge is mixed with hesitation is repelled. End of al-Ujhuri.
(3) His statement: 'and if he does them, he has sixty' — that is, in Allah's knowledge that if he does them, he has sixty years. The meaning of that is that Allah Most High knows that making his lifespan sixty years is contingent upon his obedience that is definitively occurring in Allah's knowledge, and by this, the suspicion that Allah's knowledge is mixed with hesitation is repelled. End of al-Ujhuri.
Source pages p. 328

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the concept of increase in lifespan. The author begins by explaining that the increase can be understood in multiple ways: either as an increase in goodness and blessing, or as an increase relative to what is written in the angels' scrolls. He provides an example: the scrolls may record Zayd's lifespan as fifty years absolutely, but in God's knowledge, it is restricted based on whether Zayd performs certain acts of obedience. If God knows that Zayd will perform them, his lifespan becomes sixty years. The author then discusses the verse from Surat al-Ra'd about erasing and confirming, distinguishing between the 'Mother of the Book' (Umm al-Kitab), which is God's eternal knowledge that never changes, and the Preserved Tablet (al-Lawh al-Mahfuz), which is subject to erasure and confirmation, similar to the angels' scrolls. Some scholars interpret Umm al-Kitab as the Preserved Tablet itself, but the author notes that the preponderant view is that it is God's knowledge. The footnotes elaborate on the restriction concept, emphasizing that God's knowledge is not subject to hesitation or change; the restriction is simply a recognition of what would happen under different conditions. The hadith about maintaining family ties is cited as evidence that actions can affect what is recorded in the angels' scrolls, but not God's eternal knowledge.

اللوح المحفوظ

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Umm al-Kitab and the Preserved Tablet are the same thing.
Correction: Umm al-Kitab is God's unchanging knowledge, while the Preserved Tablet can undergo erasure and confirmation.

Checkpoint

A) It is the Preserved Tablet.
B) It is God's eternal knowledge.
C) It is the angels' scrolls.
D) It is the Quran.

Key Takeaway
Umm al-Kitab is God's immutable knowledge, while the Preserved Tablet can undergo erasure and confirmation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God's knowledge is unchanging, but the Preserved Tablet can be altered by your actions, what does that tell you about the power of sincere repentance? Is there a sin you have been avoiding turning from, knowing that your record can be rewritten by Allah's mercy?
?
The verse says Allah erases and confirms what He wills. Does this truth make you feel more accountable or more hopeful? How will this change the way you pray for your future?
?
Consider the difference between God's immutable knowledge and the changeable decrees. How does this affect your trust in Allah's wisdom when your plans change or when you face unexpected trials? Write down one specific instance where you will surrender to His decree, trusting that His knowledge is perfect.

Evil Deeds: Punishment and Forgiveness
The author explains the punishment for evil deeds being equal and the possibility of forgiveness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Allah punishes evil deeds by their like but may forgive them except for disbelief, and that evil deeds can transfer to others in cases of injustice.

Core Idea
Evil deeds are punished equally, but Allah may forgive—except for disbelief.

This lesson begins with the poet's line stating two principles: evil deeds are requited by their like, and good deeds are multiplied by grace. The commentary first clarifies that the punishment for evil deeds is equal, but Allah may forgive them unless they are disbelief. Additionally, the definition of evil deeds and the scenario of transferring good deeds to satisfy the rights of others are explained.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening line and its explanation
Read the Arabic line and the commentary on 'evil deeds with Him are by the like'. Understand the meaning of equal punishment and possibility of forgiveness.
Notice the condition: unless it is disbelief.
2
Understand the definition of evil deeds
Learn what constitutes an evil deed according to the Law: anything for which the doer is blameworthy, minor or major. Also the reason it is called 'sayyi'a'.
3
Examine the transfer of deeds in oppression
Read the scenario where a wrongdoer's good deeds are given to the oppressed, and if exhausted, the oppressed's evil deeds are placed on the wrongdoer. This shows justice even after good deeds are gone.
This is a key point about divine justice.

فَالسَّيِّئَاتُ عِنْدَهُ بِالْمِثْلِ وَالْحَسَنَاتُ ضُوعِفَتْ بِالْفَضْلِ
قوله : فَالسَّيِّئَاتُ عِنْدَهُ بِالْمِثْلِ ) أَيْ : جَزَاؤُهَا عِنْدَهُ تَعَالَى مُقَدَّرٌ بِمِثْلِهَا ) ، إِنْ جَازَاهُ عَلَيْهَا، وَلَهُ أَنْ يَعْفُوَ عَنْهَا إِنْ لَمْ تَكُنْ كُفْرًا، وَإِلَّا خُلِّدَ فِي النَّارِ، وَالسَّيِّئَاتُ جَمْعُ سَيِّئَةٍ؛ مَا يُذَمُّ فَاعِلُهُ شَرْعًا ، صَغِيرَةً كَانَتْ أَوْ كَبِيرَةً، وَسُمِّيَتْ سَيِّئَةً؛ لِأَنَّ فَاعِلَهَا يَسَاءُ عِنْدَ الْمُقَابَلَةِ عَلَيْهَا يَوْمَ الْقِيَامَةِ، وَالْمُرَادُ الَّتِي عَمِلَهَا الْعَبْدُ حَقِيقَةً أَوْ حُكْمًا بِأَنْ طُرِحَتْ عَلَيْهِ لِظُلَامَةِ الْغَيْرِ بَعْدَ نَفَادِ حَسَنَاتِهِ، فَإِنَّهُ يُؤْخَذُ مِنْ حَسَنَاتِ الظَّالِمِ وَيُعْطَى لِلْمَظْلُومِ، فَإِذَا نَفِدَتْ حَسَنَاتُ الظَّالِمِ طُرِحَ عَلَيْهِ مِنْ سَيِّئَاتِ الْمَظْلُومِ، ثُمَّ قُذِفَ بِالظَّالِمِ فِي النَّارِ . وَقوله: (وَالْحَسَنَاتُ ضُوعِفَتْ بِالْفَضْلِ) أَيْ : ضَاعَفَهَا اللهُ تَعَالَى بِفَضْلِهِ لَا وُجُوبًا عَلَيْهِ، وَالْحَسَنَاتُ جَمْعُ حَسَنَةٍ؛ وَهِيَ مَا يُمْدَحُ فَاعِلُهُ شَرْعًا، وَسُمِّيَتْ حَسَنَةٌ لِحُسْنِ وَجْهِ صَاحِبِهَا عِنْدَ رُؤْيَتِهَا يَوْمَ الْقِيَامَةِ .
وَالْمُرَادُ الْحَسَنَاتُ الْمَقْبُولَةُ الْأَصْلِيَّةُ الْمَعْمُولَةُ لِلْعَبْدِ أَوْ مَا فِي حُكْمِهَا بِأَنْ عَمِلَهَا عَنْهُ غَيْرُهُ، كَمَا إِذَا تَصَدَّقَ غَيْرُكَ عَنْكَ بِصَدَقَةٍ لَا الْمَأْخُوذَةَ فِي نَظِيرِ ظُلَامَةٍ، فَخَرَجَ بِــ (الْمَقْبُولَةِ) الْمَرْدُودَةُ بِنَحْوِ رِيَاءٍ فَلَا ثَوَابَ فِيهَا أَصْلًا، وَبِ (الْأَصْلِيَّةِ) الْحَاصِلَةُ بِالتَّضْعِيفِ (۲) فَلَا تُضَاعَفُ ثَانِيًا، وَبِ (الْمَعْمُولَةِ أَوْ مَا فِي حُكْمِهَا) الْحَسَنَةُ الَّتِي هَمَّ بِهَا، فَتُكْتَبُ وَاحِدَةً مِنْ غَيْرِ تَضْعِيفٍ، وَكَذَلِكَ إِذَا صَمَّمَ عَلَى الْمَعْصِيَةِ ثُمَّ تَرَكَهَا، فَلَهُ حَسَنَةٌ مِنْ غَيْرِ مُضَاعَفَةٍ (١) وَبِقَوْلِنَا : (لَا) الْمَأْخُوذَةَ فِي نَظِيرِ (ظُلَامَةِ) الْحَسَنَةَ (۲) الَّتِي يَأْخُذُهَا الْمَظْلُومُ مِنْ ظَالِمِهِ فَلَا تُضَاعَفُ. وَالتَّضْعِيفُ مِنْ خَصَائِصِ هَذِهِ الْأُمَّةِ، وَأَمَّا غَيْرُهَا مِنَ الْأُمَمِ فَكَانَتْ حَسَنَتُهُمْ بِحَسَنَةٍ وَاحِدَةٍ وَأَقَلُّ مَرَاتِبِ التَّضْعِيفِ عَشَرَةٌ (۳) ، وَقَدْ تُضَاعَفُ إِلَى سَبْعِينَ إِلَى سَبْعِمِائَةٍ أَوْ أَكْثَرَ مِنْ غَيْرِ انْتِهَاءٍ إِلَى حَدٍّ تَقِفُ عِنْدَهُ ) ، وَتَفَاوُتُ مَرَاتِبِ التَّضْعِيفِ بِحَسَبِ مَا يَقْتَرِنُ بِالْحَسَنَةِ مِنَ الْإِخْلَاصِ وَحُسْنِ النِّيَّةِ .
And evil deeds with Him are by the like, and good deeds are multiplied by grace. He said: 'Evil deeds with Him are by the like' meaning: their recompense with Him, exalted, is estimated by their like, if He punishes them, and He may forgive them if they are not unbelief, otherwise he will be eternally in the Fire. Evil deeds (sayyi'at) is plural of evil deed (sayyi'a): that for which the doer is blameworthy according to the Law, whether minor or major. It is called evil deed because its doer will be distressed upon being confronted with it on the Day of Judgment. What is meant are those which the servant actually committed or in effect, such as being placed upon him due to a wrong done to another after his good deeds are exhausted. Then from the good deeds of the oppressor are taken and given to the oppressed. When the good deeds of the oppressor are exhausted, from the evil deeds of the oppressed are placed on him, then the oppressor is thrown into the Fire. And His saying: 'And good deeds are multiplied by grace' meaning: God multiplied them by His grace, not as an obligation upon Him. Good deeds (hasanat) is plural of good deed (hasana): that for which the doer is praised according to the Law. It is called good deed because of the beauty of its doer's face when seeing it on the Day of Judgment. And what is meant are the accepted, original good deeds actually performed by the servant or those in their ruling, such as when someone else gives charity on your behalf, not those taken in exchange for a wrong. So excluded by 'accepted' (al-maqbula) are those rejected due to hypocrisy, in which there is no reward at all. By 'original' (al-asliyya) are those resulting from multiplication (2), so they are not multiplied a second time. By 'performed or in its ruling' (al-ma'mula aw ma fi hukmiha) is the good deed that one intended, then it is recorded as one without multiplication. Likewise, if one resolved upon a sin then abandoned it, he has a good deed without multiplication (1). And by our saying 'not' (la) is the good deed taken in exchange for a wrong (2) that the oppressed takes from his oppressor, so it is not multiplied. Multiplication is a characteristic of this community alone. As for other communities, their good deed was one single good deed. The least level of multiplication is ten (3), and it may be multiplied to seventy, to seven hundred, or more without ending at a limit at which it stops. And the levels of multiplication vary according to what accompanies the good deed of sincerity and good intention.
Source pages p. 354

Commentary
This passage is an explanation of a line from the poem concerning the divine recompense for deeds. The author begins by stating the line: 'And evil deeds with Him are by the like, and good deeds are multiplied by grace.' He then comments on each part. First, he explains that evil deeds are punished by a like punishment if God chooses to punish them, but He may forgive them unless they are unbelief, in which case the doer is eternally in the Fire. He defines 'evil deed' as any act for which the doer is blameworthy according to the Law, minor or major. It is called 'evil deed' because the doer will be distressed when confronted with it on the Day of Judgment. The author clarifies that the evil deeds meant are those actually committed by the servant or those placed upon him due to a wrong he did to another, after his own good deeds are exhausted. In that case, the oppressor's good deeds are given to the oppressed, and if they are exhausted, the oppressed's evil deeds are placed on the oppressor, then the oppressor is thrown into the Fire. Next, he explains the second part: 'good deeds are multiplied by grace,' meaning that God multiplies them by His grace, not out of obligation. He defines 'good deed' as any act for which the doer is praised according to the Law, called so because of the beauty of its doer's face when seeing it on the Day of Judgment. The author then details the types of good deeds that are subject to multiplication. The intended good deeds are the 'accepted, original' ones actually performed by the servant or those in their ruling, such as charity given by another on one's behalf. Excluded are: (a) rejected deeds due to hypocrisy—these have no reward; (b) original deeds that are themselves the result of multiplication—they are not multiplied again; (c) good deeds merely intended—they are recorded as one without multiplication, similarly if one resolves on a sin then abandons it. Also excluded are good deeds taken in exchange for a wrong, i.e., when the oppressed takes good deeds from the oppressor—these are not multiplied. Multiplication is a distinctive feature of this Muslim community; other communities had their good deeds rewarded with a single good deed. The minimum multiplication is tenfold, and it can increase to seventy, seven hundred, or more without limit. The variation in multiplication depends on the sincerity and good intention accompanying the good deed.

مضاعفة
فضل
جزاء
ظلامة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that Allah must punish every evil deed without exception.
Correction: The passage clarifies that Allah may forgive evil deeds except those of disbelief. Punishment is not automatic.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what happens to a person's evil deeds if they are not unbelief?
A) They are always punished by a like punishment.
B) God may forgive them if He wills.
C) They are multiplied like good deeds.
D) They are recorded but not punished.

Key Takeaway
Evil deeds are punished by their like, but Allah may forgive except for disbelief, and the oppressor may bear the burden of the oppressed's evil deeds if his own good deeds are exhausted.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you commit a sin, do you assume Allah will punish you equally, or do you rely on His forgiveness? How does that affect your motivation to repent sincerely?
?
The passage describes a terrifying scenario: if your good deeds run out, you may bear the evil deeds of those you wronged. Have you truly considered the weight of your injustices against others? What one relationship do you need to make right today?
?
The only sin that cannot be forgiven is disbelief. Do you have any doubt or complacency about your faith? What would it take to strengthen your certainty in Allah's mercy and justice?

Good Deeds Multiplied by Grace
The author explains the multiplication of good deeds by grace, its conditions, and its exclusivity to this community.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that good deeds are multiplied by Allah's grace, not obligation, and that multiplication is exclusive to this community and varies based on sincerity.

Core Idea
Good deeds are multiplied by Allah's grace, starting at tenfold and increasing without limit.

In this lesson, we explore the second part of the line: good deeds are multiplied by grace. The commentator explains that multiplication is a favor from Allah, not an obligation. He defines good deeds and outlines the conditions for multiplication: they must be accepted, original, and performed by the servant or on his behalf. Multiplication is a unique blessing for this community, with the minimum being tenfold and no upper limit, depending on sincerity.

Guided Path
1
Read the explanation of multiplication
Read the commentary on 'good deeds are multiplied by grace'. Understand that multiplication is by Allah's grace, not because He is obliged.
This emphasizes Allah's generosity.
2
Learn the definition of good deeds
Find the definition of 'hasana' (good deed) and why it is called that.
3
Identify the conditions for multiplication
The passage lists four exclusions: rejected deeds, deeds resulting from multiplication, intended deeds, and deeds taken in exchange for a wrong. Understand each.
These conditions show that not all good deeds are multiplied equally.
4
Understand that multiplication is exclusive to this community
Read the part about multiplication being a characteristic of the Muslim community, with a minimum of ten, and no limit.
This highlights the special mercy of Allah upon this ummah.

فَالسَّيِّئَاتُ عِنْدَهُ بِالْمِثْلِ وَالْحَسَنَاتُ ضُوعِفَتْ بِالْفَضْلِ
قوله : فَالسَّيِّئَاتُ عِنْدَهُ بِالْمِثْلِ ) أَيْ : جَزَاؤُهَا عِنْدَهُ تَعَالَى مُقَدَّرٌ بِمِثْلِهَا ) ، إِنْ جَازَاهُ عَلَيْهَا، وَلَهُ أَنْ يَعْفُوَ عَنْهَا إِنْ لَمْ تَكُنْ كُفْرًا، وَإِلَّا خُلِّدَ فِي النَّارِ، وَالسَّيِّئَاتُ جَمْعُ سَيِّئَةٍ؛ مَا يُذَمُّ فَاعِلُهُ شَرْعًا ، صَغِيرَةً كَانَتْ أَوْ كَبِيرَةً، وَسُمِّيَتْ سَيِّئَةً؛ لِأَنَّ فَاعِلَهَا يَسَاءُ عِنْدَ الْمُقَابَلَةِ عَلَيْهَا يَوْمَ الْقِيَامَةِ، وَالْمُرَادُ الَّتِي عَمِلَهَا الْعَبْدُ حَقِيقَةً أَوْ حُكْمًا بِأَنْ طُرِحَتْ عَلَيْهِ لِظُلَامَةِ الْغَيْرِ بَعْدَ نَفَادِ حَسَنَاتِهِ، فَإِنَّهُ يُؤْخَذُ مِنْ حَسَنَاتِ الظَّالِمِ وَيُعْطَى لِلْمَظْلُومِ، فَإِذَا نَفِدَتْ حَسَنَاتُ الظَّالِمِ طُرِحَ عَلَيْهِ مِنْ سَيِّئَاتِ الْمَظْلُومِ، ثُمَّ قُذِفَ بِالظَّالِمِ فِي النَّارِ . وَقوله: (وَالْحَسَنَاتُ ضُوعِفَتْ بِالْفَضْلِ) أَيْ : ضَاعَفَهَا اللهُ تَعَالَى بِفَضْلِهِ لَا وُجُوبًا عَلَيْهِ، وَالْحَسَنَاتُ جَمْعُ حَسَنَةٍ؛ وَهِيَ مَا يُمْدَحُ فَاعِلُهُ شَرْعًا، وَسُمِّيَتْ حَسَنَةٌ لِحُسْنِ وَجْهِ صَاحِبِهَا عِنْدَ رُؤْيَتِهَا يَوْمَ الْقِيَامَةِ .
وَالْمُرَادُ الْحَسَنَاتُ الْمَقْبُولَةُ الْأَصْلِيَّةُ الْمَعْمُولَةُ لِلْعَبْدِ أَوْ مَا فِي حُكْمِهَا بِأَنْ عَمِلَهَا عَنْهُ غَيْرُهُ، كَمَا إِذَا تَصَدَّقَ غَيْرُكَ عَنْكَ بِصَدَقَةٍ لَا الْمَأْخُوذَةَ فِي نَظِيرِ ظُلَامَةٍ، فَخَرَجَ بِــ (الْمَقْبُولَةِ) الْمَرْدُودَةُ بِنَحْوِ رِيَاءٍ فَلَا ثَوَابَ فِيهَا أَصْلًا، وَبِ (الْأَصْلِيَّةِ) الْحَاصِلَةُ بِالتَّضْعِيفِ (۲) فَلَا تُضَاعَفُ ثَانِيًا، وَبِ (الْمَعْمُولَةِ أَوْ مَا فِي حُكْمِهَا) الْحَسَنَةُ الَّتِي هَمَّ بِهَا، فَتُكْتَبُ وَاحِدَةً مِنْ غَيْرِ تَضْعِيفٍ، وَكَذَلِكَ إِذَا صَمَّمَ عَلَى الْمَعْصِيَةِ ثُمَّ تَرَكَهَا، فَلَهُ حَسَنَةٌ مِنْ غَيْرِ مُضَاعَفَةٍ (١) وَبِقَوْلِنَا : (لَا) الْمَأْخُوذَةَ فِي نَظِيرِ (ظُلَامَةِ) الْحَسَنَةَ (۲) الَّتِي يَأْخُذُهَا الْمَظْلُومُ مِنْ ظَالِمِهِ فَلَا تُضَاعَفُ. وَالتَّضْعِيفُ مِنْ خَصَائِصِ هَذِهِ الْأُمَّةِ، وَأَمَّا غَيْرُهَا مِنَ الْأُمَمِ فَكَانَتْ حَسَنَتُهُمْ بِحَسَنَةٍ وَاحِدَةٍ وَأَقَلُّ مَرَاتِبِ التَّضْعِيفِ عَشَرَةٌ (۳) ، وَقَدْ تُضَاعَفُ إِلَى سَبْعِينَ إِلَى سَبْعِمِائَةٍ أَوْ أَكْثَرَ مِنْ غَيْرِ انْتِهَاءٍ إِلَى حَدٍّ تَقِفُ عِنْدَهُ ) ، وَتَفَاوُتُ مَرَاتِبِ التَّضْعِيفِ بِحَسَبِ مَا يَقْتَرِنُ بِالْحَسَنَةِ مِنَ الْإِخْلَاصِ وَحُسْنِ النِّيَّةِ .
And evil deeds with Him are by the like, and good deeds are multiplied by grace. He said: 'Evil deeds with Him are by the like' meaning: their recompense with Him, exalted, is estimated by their like, if He punishes them, and He may forgive them if they are not unbelief, otherwise he will be eternally in the Fire. Evil deeds (sayyi'at) is plural of evil deed (sayyi'a): that for which the doer is blameworthy according to the Law, whether minor or major. It is called evil deed because its doer will be distressed upon being confronted with it on the Day of Judgment. What is meant are those which the servant actually committed or in effect, such as being placed upon him due to a wrong done to another after his good deeds are exhausted. Then from the good deeds of the oppressor are taken and given to the oppressed. When the good deeds of the oppressor are exhausted, from the evil deeds of the oppressed are placed on him, then the oppressor is thrown into the Fire. And His saying: 'And good deeds are multiplied by grace' meaning: God multiplied them by His grace, not as an obligation upon Him. Good deeds (hasanat) is plural of good deed (hasana): that for which the doer is praised according to the Law. It is called good deed because of the beauty of its doer's face when seeing it on the Day of Judgment. And what is meant are the accepted, original good deeds actually performed by the servant or those in their ruling, such as when someone else gives charity on your behalf, not those taken in exchange for a wrong. So excluded by 'accepted' (al-maqbula) are those rejected due to hypocrisy, in which there is no reward at all. By 'original' (al-asliyya) are those resulting from multiplication (2), so they are not multiplied a second time. By 'performed or in its ruling' (al-ma'mula aw ma fi hukmiha) is the good deed that one intended, then it is recorded as one without multiplication. Likewise, if one resolved upon a sin then abandoned it, he has a good deed without multiplication (1). And by our saying 'not' (la) is the good deed taken in exchange for a wrong (2) that the oppressed takes from his oppressor, so it is not multiplied. Multiplication is a characteristic of this community alone. As for other communities, their good deed was one single good deed. The least level of multiplication is ten (3), and it may be multiplied to seventy, to seven hundred, or more without ending at a limit at which it stops. And the levels of multiplication vary according to what accompanies the good deed of sincerity and good intention.
Source pages p. 354

Commentary
This passage is an explanation of a line from the poem concerning the divine recompense for deeds. The author begins by stating the line: 'And evil deeds with Him are by the like, and good deeds are multiplied by grace.' He then comments on each part. First, he explains that evil deeds are punished by a like punishment if God chooses to punish them, but He may forgive them unless they are unbelief, in which case the doer is eternally in the Fire. He defines 'evil deed' as any act for which the doer is blameworthy according to the Law, minor or major. It is called 'evil deed' because the doer will be distressed when confronted with it on the Day of Judgment. The author clarifies that the evil deeds meant are those actually committed by the servant or those placed upon him due to a wrong he did to another, after his own good deeds are exhausted. In that case, the oppressor's good deeds are given to the oppressed, and if they are exhausted, the oppressed's evil deeds are placed on the oppressor, then the oppressor is thrown into the Fire. Next, he explains the second part: 'good deeds are multiplied by grace,' meaning that God multiplies them by His grace, not out of obligation. He defines 'good deed' as any act for which the doer is praised according to the Law, called so because of the beauty of its doer's face when seeing it on the Day of Judgment. The author then details the types of good deeds that are subject to multiplication. The intended good deeds are the 'accepted, original' ones actually performed by the servant or those in their ruling, such as charity given by another on one's behalf. Excluded are: (a) rejected deeds due to hypocrisy—these have no reward; (b) original deeds that are themselves the result of multiplication—they are not multiplied again; (c) good deeds merely intended—they are recorded as one without multiplication, similarly if one resolves on a sin then abandons it. Also excluded are good deeds taken in exchange for a wrong, i.e., when the oppressed takes good deeds from the oppressor—these are not multiplied. Multiplication is a distinctive feature of this Muslim community; other communities had their good deeds rewarded with a single good deed. The minimum multiplication is tenfold, and it can increase to seventy, seven hundred, or more without limit. The variation in multiplication depends on the sincerity and good intention accompanying the good deed.

Key Terms
حسنة
مضاعفة
فضل
إخلاص
نية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that Allah is obliged to multiply good deeds.
Correction: The passage clearly states that multiplication is by Allah's grace, not obligation.

Checkpoint
What is the minimum multiplication for good deeds in this community?
A) One
B) Ten
C) Seventy
D) Seven hundred

Key Takeaway
Good deeds are multiplied by Allah's grace (not obligation), with a minimum of tenfold and no upper limit, depending on sincerity, and this multiplication is a special mercy for the Muslim community.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you perform a good deed, do you secretly calculate the reward it might bring, or do you focus solely on the act for the sake of Allah? How does the knowledge that multiplication is by grace alone change your attitude?
?
The source says that intending a good deed but not performing it only gives one hasanah without multiplication. Have you ever relied on your intentions alone as if they were deeds? How can you act on your intentions more consistently?
?
Recognizing that multiplication is a specific mercy for this ummah, do you feel a sense of gratitude and responsibility? How can you embody that gratitude in your daily worship?

The Ash'ari View on the Delay of Threat
Al-Bajuri explains the Ash'ari justification for the possibility of delay of divine threat.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Ash'ari school believes that God can delay threatened punishment, based on the condition of His will.

Core Idea
God's threats are conditioned on His will, so punishment can be delayed.

This passage introduces the Ash'ari principle that divine threats are conditional upon God's will. Al-Bajuri explains that just as a generous person might say 'I will punish you' meaning 'if I will', so too God's warnings are not absolute obligations. This has significant implications for understanding divine justice and mercy.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation to understand the argument.
2
Focus on the conditional statement
Notice how the example of a generous person is used to illustrate the condition of will.
3
Connect to Ash'ari theology
Understand that this leads to the conclusion that God is not obligated to punish every sinner; He may forgive or delay.
This is a key difference from Mu'tazili views.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما على طريقة الأشاعرة من أنه يجوز تخلف الوعيد؛ لأنه على تقدير المشيئة، كما هو عادة الكريم، فإنه إذا قال : إذا فعل زيد كذا أعاقبه . . كان المراد أعاقبه إن شئت، فلا يجب تعذيب بعض العصاة؛ لجواز تخلف الوعيد، نعم قد ورد تعذيب بعض الموحدين والشفاعة فيهم، لكن لا يعمُّ الأنواع كلَّها . قوله : (ثُمَّ الخُلُوْدُ مُجْتَنَبْ) أي: ثم خلود من أراد الله تعذيبه من عصاة المؤمنين مُجْتَتَبٌ وقوعه، فلا نقول به . والحاصل أن الناس على قسمين : مؤمنٌ ، وكافر؛ فالكافر مخلد في النار إجماعاً، والمؤمن على قسمين: طائع وعاص ; فالطائع في الجنة إجماعاً، والعاصي على قسمين تائب، وغيرُ تائب؛ فالتائب في الجنة إجماعاً وغير التائب في المشيئة، وعلى تقدير عذابِهِ لا يُخلَّد في النار.
And as for the Ash'ari way, that it is permissible for the threat to be delayed, because it is on the condition of willing, as is the custom of the Generous One, for if He says: 'If Zayd does such-and-such, I will punish him', the intended meaning is 'I will punish him if I will'. So it is not necessary to punish some disobedient ones, due to the permissibility of delay of the threat. Yes, punishment of some monotheists and intercession for them has been reported, but it does not encompass all types. His saying: (Then eternity is avoided) meaning: then the eternity of those whom God wills to punish among disobedient believers is averted in occurrence, so we do not assert it. The summary is that people are of two types: believer and disbeliever. The disbeliever is eternally in Hell by consensus. The believer is of two types: obedient and disobedient. The obedient is in Paradise by consensus. The disobedient is of two types: repentant and non-repentant. The repentant is in Paradise by consensus, and the non-repentant is under the will (of God), and if punishment is decreed for him, he is not eternally in Hell.
Source pages p. 384

Commentary
This passage is a theological argument explaining the Ash'ari stance on divine threats. It begins by stating that according to the Ash'ari school, it is permissible for God to delay the punishment He threatens, because such threats are implicitly conditioned on His will, just as a generous person might say 'I will punish you' meaning 'if I will'. This means that God is not obliged to punish every disobedient believer; He may forgive or intercede. The author then glosses the poem's line 'Then eternity is avoided'—the eternity in Hell for disobedient believers is not inevitable; it can be averted. He then presents a classification: people are divided into believers and disbelievers. Disbelievers are eternally damned by consensus. Believers are further divided into obedient and disobedient; the obedient enter Paradise. Among the disobedient, those who repent enter Paradise; those who do not repent are under God's will—He may punish them temporarily but they will not be eternally in Hell. This reinforces the Ash'ari doctrine that no believer will suffer eternal punishment.

Key Terms
تخلف الوعيد
المشيئة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That God must always carry out His threats immediately without exception.
Correction: Ash'ari theology holds that threats are conditional on God's will; He may delay or forgive.

Checkpoint
According to the Ash'ari view, why is it permissible for God to delay threatened punishment?
A) Because God is not just.
B) Because threats are on the condition of His will.
C) Because punishment is always immediate.
D) Because God is not powerful.

Key Takeaway
The Ash'ari school teaches that divine threats are conditional on God's will, allowing for the possibility of forgiveness or delayed punishment.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read that God's threats are conditional, do you rely on that condition to excuse your own disobedience? How does that make you feel about your accountability before God?
?
If you knew that a sin you commit might be punished but might also be forgiven, does that knowledge change the urgency with which you seek repentance? What is one specific thing you will do today to act on that urgency?
?
This lesson says punishment of some monotheists has been reported. Does the possibility that you could be among those punished shake your complacency? What concrete step can you take to ensure you are not among the punished?

The Categories of People and Their Fates
Al-Bajuri classifies people into categories and states their eternal fates by consensus and Ash'ari doctrine.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the classification of people into believers and disbelievers, and the fate of each subgroup according to Ash'ari consensus.

Core Idea
No believer suffers eternal punishment; only disbelievers are eternally in Hell.

After establishing the principle of delay, Al-Bajuri presents a clear classification of people based on faith and obedience. This classification answers the question of who receives eternal punishment and who does not. It is a key element of Ash'ari soteriology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two main categories
People are divided into believer and disbeliever. Disbelievers are eternally in Hell by consensus.
2
Subdivide believers
Believers are obedient or disobedient. Obedient believers are in Paradise by consensus.
3
Subdivide disobedient believers
Disobedient believers are repentant or non-repentant. Repentant are in Paradise by consensus.
4
Non-repentant fate
Non-repentant believers are under God's will; if punished, it is not eternal.
This is a key Ash'ari doctrine: no believer will be eternally punished.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And as for the Ash'ari way, that it is permissible for the threat to be delayed, because it is on the condition of willing, as is the custom of the Generous One, for if He says: 'If Zayd does such-and-such, I will punish him', the intended meaning is 'I will punish him if I will'. Yes, punishment of some monotheists and intercession for them has been reported, but it does not encompass all types. The obedient is in Paradise by consensus. The disobedient is of two types: repentant and non-repentant. The repentant is in Paradise by consensus, and the non-repentant is under the will (of God), and if punishment is decreed for him, he is not eternally in Hell.
Source pages p. 384

Commentary
This passage is a theological argument explaining the Ash'ari stance on divine threats. It begins by stating that according to the Ash'ari school, it is permissible for God to delay the punishment He threatens, because such threats are implicitly conditioned on His will, just as a generous person might say 'I will punish you' meaning 'if I will'. Checkpoint
According to the classification in this passage, what is the fate of a non-repentant disobedient believer?

The Perpetual Blessings: Grammar and Theology
Grammatical and theological explanation of 'al-da'im'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the grammatical analysis of 'al-da'im' (the perpetual) and why perpetuity is attributed to the reward of the blessings, not their utterance.

Core Idea
Perpetuity of blessings refers to their virtue, not the words themselves.

The commentator begins by parsing the word 'al-da'im' (perpetual) from the poem. He explores two possible grammatical constructions and clarifies a subtle theological point: the blessings are called perpetual because of their enduring reward, even though the spoken words are temporary.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and translation. Notice the two grammatical possibilities for 'al-da'im'.
2
Identify the grammatical options
The commentator says 'al-da'im' could describe both prayer and peace, or just 'peace' with 'prayer's adjective omitted. Understand the reasoning.
The omitted construction is less common.
3
Grasp the theological nuance
Why is perpetuity not about the spoken words? Because words are accidents that pass away. Perpetuity is about virtue and reward.
This is a key point.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (الدَّائِمُ) أي : كلُّ منهما، ويحتمل أن يكون صفة للسلام، ويكون المصنف حذف من الصلاة نظيره والتقدير ثم الصلاة الدائمة والسلام الدائم ؛ فيكون في كلامه الأول لدلالة الثاني، وإن كان خلاف الغالب ؛ وهو الحذف من الثاني لدلالة الأول. ولا يخفى أن الدوام باعتبار فضلهما وثمرتهما لا باعتبار لفظهما ؛ لأنهما عَرَضان ينقضيان بمجرد النطق بهما .
قوله : ( عَلَى نَبِيِّ) أي : كائنان على نبي .
وقوله : (دَأْبُهُ المَرَاحِمُ) جملةٌ من مبتدإ وخبرٍ صفةٌ لـ (نبي)؛ أي: على نبي موصوف بأن دأبه المراحم . ومعنى الدأب العادة والمراحم جمع مرحمة بمعنى الرحمة، فالمعنى: عادته المستمرة الرحمة للعالمين. ففيه تلميح لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَمَا أَرْسَلْنَاكَ إِلَّا رَحْمَةً لِلْعَالَمِينَ [الأنبياء: ۱۰۷] .
وقوله : (مُحَمَّدٍ) بدل من (نبي) أو عطف بيان عليه زاده الله تشريفاً وتكريماً لديه، وإنما ترك الناظم وصفه بالسيادة لضرورة النظم، وإلا فيستحبُّ وصفه بالسيادة استعمالاً للأدب، كما قاله الجلال المحلي في الصلاة وغيرها. وأما حديث: لا تُسيّدوني في صلاتكم فقال السيوطي: لا أصل له
وروى أبو داود (١٤٨١) من حديث فضالة ابن عبيد عن النبي : إذا صلى أحدكم فليبدأ بتحميد ربه والثناء عليه، ثم يُصلي على النبي ، ثم يدعو بما شاء». قال أبو سليمان الداراني رحمه الله : من أراد أن يسأل الله حاجةٌ فليبدأ بالصلاة على النبي ، ثم يسأله حاجته، ثم يختم بالصلاة على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ، فإن الله يقبل الصلاتين، وهو أكرم من أن يدع ما بينهما .
(۱) قوله : (ولا يخفى ... إلخ) لا حاجة إلى هذا ؛ لأن الصلاة في كلام المصنف بمعنى الرحمة، والسلام في كلامه بمعنى التحية، وهما موصوفان بالدوام، ومعنى كلام المصنف : ثم الرحمة والتحية الدائمتان على نبي. انتهى أفاده الأمير. انتهى أجهوري.
His saying: (the perpetual) means: each of them (i.e., prayer and peace). It is possible that it is an adjective for peace, and that the author omitted its counterpart from prayer, the estimation being: then the perpetual prayer and the perpetual peace. So in his statement, the first indicates the second, although it is contrary to the usual pattern, which is omission from the second indicated by the first. And it is not hidden that perpetuity is with respect to their virtue and reward, not with respect to their utterance, because they are accidents that pass away upon mere pronunciation.
His saying: (upon a Prophet) means: both are upon a Prophet.
His saying: (whose habit is mercies) is a sentence of subject and predicate that is an adjective for 'Prophet'; i.e., upon a Prophet described by the fact that his habit is mercies. The meaning of 'da'b' is habit, and 'al-marahim' is the plural of 'marhama' meaning mercy. So the meaning: his constant habit is mercy for the worlds. In it is a hint to His saying, Exalted: 'And We have not sent you except as a mercy for the worlds' [al-Anbiya: 107].
His saying: (Muhammad) is a substitute for 'Prophet' or a clarifying conjunction. May God honor and venerate him. The author only omitted describing him with 'sayyid' due to poetic necessity; otherwise, it is recommended to describe him with 'sayyid' as an expression of respect, as al-Jalal al-Mahalli said concerning prayer and other matters. As for the hadith: 'Do not call me sayyid in your prayer,' al-Suyuti said: it has no basis.
And Abu Dawud narrated (1481) from the hadith of Fadala ibn 'Ubayd from the Prophet: 'When one of you prays, let him begin with the praise of his Lord and exaltation of Him, then send prayers upon the Prophet, then supplicate as he wishes.' Abu Sulayman al-Darani said: Whoever wants to ask God for a need, let him begin with prayer upon the Prophet, then ask his need, then conclude with prayer upon the Prophet, for God accepts the two prayers and is too generous to abandon what is between them.
Footnote (1): His saying: ('And it is not hidden...' etc.) There is no need for this, because 'prayer' in the author's speech means mercy, and 'peace' in his speech means greeting, and both are described as perpetual. The meaning of the author's speech is: then the perpetual mercy and greeting upon a Prophet. End of al-Amir. End of al-Ajhuri.
Source pages p. 427

Commentary
This passage provides detailed grammatical and theological analysis of the poem's description. First, the word 'al-da'im' (the perpetual) is explained as applying to both prayer and peace; it is possible that it is an adjective for 'peace' alone with the adjective for 'prayer' implied. The perpetuity is not in the utterance itself (since words pass away) but in their virtue and reward. Then the phrase 'upon a Prophet' is straightforward. The description 'whose habit is mercies' is a nominal sentence acting as an adjective: the Prophet's constant habit is mercy for all worlds, hinting at the Quranic verse 'mercy for the worlds'. The name 'Muhammad' is grammatically a substitute or clarifying conjunction. The commentator notes that the poet omitted the title 'sayyid' (master) due to poetic meter, but it is recommended to use it out of respect; the hadith that forbids saying 'sayyid' in prayer is unfounded according to al-Suyuti. Finally, a hadith from Abu Dawud is quoted to show the virtue of beginning and ending supplication with prayer upon the Prophet, and Abu Sulayman al-Darani emphasizes that God accepts such prayers. The footnote simplifies: prayer means mercy, peace means greeting, both perpetual on the Prophet.

Key Terms
الدائم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that the blessings are perpetual because we repeat them often.
Correction: The commentator clarifies that perpetuity refers to their virtue and reward, not the frequency of utterance.

Checkpoint
Why does the commentator say the blessings are called 'perpetual'?
A) Because the words are repeated often
B) Because of their lasting virtue and reward
C) Because the Prophet lives forever
D) Because the poem says so

Key Takeaway
The attribute 'perpetual' for the blessings upon the Prophet refers to their enduring spiritual benefit, not the fleeting words.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite blessings upon the Prophet, do you truly believe that each phrase carries an eternal reward, or do you treat it as a momentary ritual? How would your heart change if you savored every syllable knowing its virtue never ends?
?
The lesson reveals that the words themselves fade instantly. Are you content with merely uttering the sound, or will you strive to send blessings with such presence that the eternal meaning transforms your soul? Commit today to one salawat with full awareness.
?
If the perpetual nature of salawat lies in their reward, not your recitation, then what does that say about your intention? Will you pause before you next invoke peace upon the Prophet and silently acknowledge that this act is not fleeting but an investment in eternal grace?

intermediate

The Prophet's Habit of Mercy and the Honorific 'Sayyid'
Commentary on the Prophet's description and the title 'sayyid'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the description of the Prophet as one whose habit is mercy, the grammatical analysis of his name, and the recommendation to call him 'sayyid'.

Core Idea
The Prophet's constant habit is mercy for all worlds, and it is recommended to honor him with the title 'sayyid'.

This passage continues the commentary on the poem's description of the Prophet. It explains the phrase 'whose habit is mercies,' links it to the Quranic verse, and then discusses the name 'Muhammad' and the omission of 'sayyid' due to poetic necessity. The commentator also quotes a hadith on the etiquette of supplication.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and translation completely. Notice the three parts: the description, the name, and the hadith.
2
Understand the description 'da'buhu al-marahim'
This phrase means his constant habit is mercy. It alludes to Quran 21:107. Reflect on the theological significance.
3
Analyze the name 'Muhammad' and the 'sayyid' discussion
Grammatically, it is a substitute or appositive. The poet omitted 'sayyid' due to meter, but it is recommended. Note the refutation of a false hadith.
4
Reflect on the supplication etiquette
The hadith teaches to begin and end supplication with praise and blessings on the Prophet. This shows the importance of sending blessings.

His saying: (the perpetual) means: each of them (i.e., prayer and peace). It is possible that it is an adjective for peace, and that the author omitted its counterpart from prayer, the estimation being: then the perpetual prayer and the perpetual peace. So in his statement, the first indicates the second, although it is contrary to the usual pattern, which is omission from the second indicated by the first. And it is not hidden that perpetuity is with respect to their virtue and reward, not with respect to their utterance, because they are accidents that pass away upon mere pronunciation.
His saying: (upon a Prophet) means: both are upon a Prophet.

The meaning of 'da'b' is habit, and 'al-marahim' is the plural of 'marhama' meaning mercy. So the meaning: his constant habit is mercy for the worlds. In it is a hint to His saying, Exalted: 'And We have not sent you except as a mercy for the worlds' [al-Anbiya: 107].
His saying: (Muhammad) is a substitute for 'Prophet' or a clarifying conjunction. May God honor and venerate him. The author only omitted describing him with 'sayyid' due to poetic necessity; otherwise, it is recommended to describe him with 'sayyid' as an expression of respect, as al-Jalal al-Mahalli said concerning prayer and other matters. As for the hadith: 'Do not call me sayyid in your prayer,' al-Suyuti said: it has no basis.
And Abu Dawud narrated (1481) from the hadith of Fadala ibn 'Ubayd from the Prophet: 'When one of you prays, let him begin with the praise of his Lord and exaltation of Him, then send prayers upon the Prophet, then supplicate as he wishes.' Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that using 'sayyid' for the Prophet is forbidden in prayer based on a hadith.
Correction: The commentator reports that al-Suyuti said that hadith has no basis, and it is recommended to use 'sayyid' out of respect.

Checkpoint
Why did the poet omit the word 'sayyid' (master) when referring to the Prophet?
A) He considered it disrespectful
B) He forgot
C) Due to poetic necessity
D) The Prophet forbade it

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's essential attribute is mercy, and honoring him with the title 'sayyid' is recommended; supplication is best framed with blessings upon him.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you last supplicated, did you consciously begin with praise of Allah and send blessings on the Prophet? If not, will you commit to doing so from now on?
?
The Prophet's constant habit is mercy for the worlds. In what specific area of your life today can you imitate that habit of mercy toward others?
?
Do you truly honor the Prophet (peace be upon him) with the respect he deserves in your daily speech and thoughts, or do you sometimes take his station lightly?
